Ticket: PFT-7957
Issue id: 201764
Module: Staff/HR
Summary: SAM people - Arbor payscaled
Role: Data manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 2
Comment: From SAMPeople - I am just getting back in touch regarding increasing pay scales in bulk, in line with government increases.

 I have had a message back from my colleague regarding this, and unfortunately, there is no way to bulk change pay scales in line with government changes; they will have to be manually updated. You can follow the advice in this help centre article to increase those pay scales.

 I can understand that this is not the outcome you were wanting, and I am really surprised that this isn't a feature in Arbor, as it sounds like this would be a great feature for lots of schools using Arbor. This would be great product feedback for our product team!

 Our team at Arbor is unable to submit suggestions on behalf of schools, as we want to ensure the full impact and needs of your school have been reflected in the suggestion. We appreciate this can be more time-consuming than you would hope, but it will help us to improve our product for all schools.

Ticket: PFT-7933
Issue id: 201687
Module: Core Student Record
Summary: Parents and schools should not be able to change "sex" field on a student's profile in Arbor
Role: Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 26
Comment: Originally on Arbor, ‚Äúgender‚Äù was the only field available to record a child‚Äôs sex. This caused issues for the school census because schools were updating this field frequently, depending on how the child wished to be identified on a given day. To address this problem the DFE changed their guidance on this and therefore, Arbor introduced a separate ‚Äúsex‚Äù field so that census data could be reported accurately. The original ‚Äúgender‚Äù field was then renamed to ‚Äúgender identity‚Äù to reflect how a student identifies within the school.

 This "sex" field should therefore NOT be changed.

 However, if the sex field can still be changed by parents or by the school, it undermines the purpose of having two separate fields. In practice, both sex and gender identity would end up showing the same information, which defeats the distinction.

 This also means the school census data is often incorrect, since the field continues to be updated and is included in the census return.

I was exploring the possiblity to add actual (eg. GCSE results) onto our Post 16 summative assessments, but I couldn't find a way to do this.

 Your team is super cool and has brilliant minds, surely there is a lot to improve, however, my tip to your team - act as software architects /engineers, but think at a typical teacher level, step into their shoes and don't step out - this is what leads your product to become a leader in the market. By the way, I work for two trusts with over 30 schools and I'm thinking 'selling' Arbor to one trust that still operates on Bromcom. But I've got to see your Assessments 2.0 in operation! It's key! Currently, I'm not enjoying operating it - it's a bit like Cybertruck - too many sharp angles. I get your logic why targets are not shown by default, however, for teachers the targets are key, even if targets should not be an influence when they enter the grades for the term. Or another feedback from other topic which is painful - it should be made easier to manage, off set unopened or incomplete registers. I know there are recommendations how to do this, but not all lessons that don't happen have a support staff cover, and I know we have the functionality to suspend the lessons, but the reality in many schools is different - we just need a better tool to cancel incomplete registers alerts on staff to do list, because they become a 'noise' and staff miss the important stuff on to do list. In other words, more elasticity, more control to schools.

 Sorry, my thoughts weren't were structure, but at least I said what was on my mind.

Ticket: PFT-7443
Issue id: 199727
Module: Communications
Summary: Session Timeout Warning for Arbor
Role: Head of IT System
Source: Sheet1 - Row 516
Comment: *Problem:*

 Users such as data managers remain logged into Arbor for extended periods while performing complex updates and routing tasks. These processes often involve critical data entry where any loss can have significant consequences.

 Currently, the 3-hour session timeout occurs without sufficient warning. When the timeout hits, users experience:

 Frozen screens during data entry or saving

 Forced re-login

 Loss of unsaved data

 Time wasted navigating back to the original screen and re-entering information

 This creates frustration and inefficiency, especially for roles that rely on uninterrupted workflows.

 *Proposed Solution:*

 Introduce a session timeout warning system that proactively alerts users before their session expires. Key features could include:

 Customisable Warning Interval: Notify users (e.g., 10‚Äì15 minutes before timeout) so they can save work or refresh the session.

 Extend Session Option: Provide a simple ‚ÄúStay Logged In‚Äù button to reset the timer without disrupting the workflow.

 Visual and Audible Alerts: Use a clear pop-up or banner notification, possibly with an optional sound alert for high-focus tasks.

 Auto-Save Integration: Where possible, implement auto-save for in-progress data to minimise loss even if the session ends.

 *Benefits*:

 Prevents unexpected data loss

 Improves user experience and trust in the platform

 Reduces time wasted on re-login and navigation

 Supports productivity for roles handling complex, time-sensitive processes

Summary: Permissions - improved management
Role: Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 561
Comment: Hi,

 I absolutely love your data retention management function!

 With over 17 years of experience in Cyber Security, I'm of the opinion that Permissions section - the strategy= policy, setting up permissions frameworks for different business roles, cascading assigned permissions, managing changes / differences by taking into account ad-hoc permissions that may have been grated to this Head of Year but not the other... scheduled annual reviews (I'm talking about ISO 9001 & 27001 related ISMS management frameworks) - all this could be optimized. Currently, it's just blurred into a sea of permissions with no clear oversight if a person with same business role has more persmissions than the other with the same business role and when it was last revied, by whom, etc.

 Also, I may have submitted the request earlier, but permission need to be more granular. I may want to assign just the tiny permission section that's associated with the permission function. Less is more from cyber security point of view and assigning permissions left and right is not the right approach. On the other hand, surely, permissions should enable business function and not restrain.

 Last but not least, I've learned that some schools have this weird thing when a teacher leaves the role, they still have access to MIS for 2 years , so to say, if they like to view how their students are doing. This is an absolute NO NO from cyber security aspect (access control). Is there a way to link permissions section to people who are marked as no longer working at school first of all to alert eg. Data Manager (in my case, I'm managing permissions, but am not the only person to have the rights in changing the permissions) and secondly, any people who leave, I should be given the option via an altert to switch their access rights to least privilege access.

 BR

 Ema

Ticket: PFT-7393
Issue id: 199488
Module: Assessments
Summary: Assessments - target vs current grade colouring rule
Role: Data Manager
Source: Sheet1 - Row 566
Comment: Hi,

 For KS3, we have overlapping colouring structure. Let me explain:

 Students on LPA (low attainment), if their grades are 1-3, they should be marked as GREEN = Expected. On the same attainment band, students with grades 4 and above should be marked as PURPLE as they are EXCEEDING.

 Students on MPA (medium attainment), if they get grades 1-4, they are below the target = YELLOW as they are EMERGING, students with grades 4-6 are GREEN - Expected and students with grades above 6 are EXCEEDING = Purple.

 Students in HPA (High attainment), if they have grades below 7, they are Emerging (below target) grades 7-9 are Expected = Green = on target.

 We need to be able to design this if we have an overlapping structure. I have noticed that currently it's not available to set an overlapping structure and also, Arbor does not allow you to have a different rule for different key stage, eg. KS3 in our case. We have set up a school rule that works perfectly for KS4 and KS5, but we don't seem to be able to set up more than one school rule.

Ticket: PFT-7282
Issue id: 199232
Module: Behaviour
Summary: Use retrospective dates for internal isolations
Role: Pastoral Administrator
Source: Sheet1 - Row 677
Comment: I need to use past dates when assigning internal isolations but this has changed so that I can only select today onwards. Is there a settings change I can make?

 See notes from my training with SBS:

 Just to update you on the internal exclusion dates that we discussed previously and I had raised with Arbor. They have confirmed as we thought that when logging/amending the exclusions you can't from this area set students for past dates. Arbor have provided their reasoning for this which will detail below.

 They have however explained there is a workaround you can use which I will also detail below. They have suggested in the meantime if you would prefer to leave feedback with Arbor about making a change to the system you can do so using the feedback options on Arbor.

 If you have any questions then please let me know.

 It is expected for Arbor to work like this; it just avoids the teachers and other staff having to scroll through load and loads of sessions the later it gets in the year. The recommended method of removing and re-adding students is by going to Students > Behaviour > Internal Exclusions > Daily Attendance, amending the date and then clicking into the exclusion. You can click on the student's name and then click Remove from Session (Screenshot attached).

 You can then use the same method to find the past intervention they need to be added to and use the +Add button.

It would be useful if the area showed current enrolments only and you could scroll down to another section that was past enrolments (this is how it shows in other areas in Arbor).

 Thanks,

Ticket: PFT-7177
Issue id: 198851
Module: Parent Portal/App
Summary: Enable Direct Communication Between Parents/Carers and Staff via the Arbor Parent App
Role: Assistant Principal - Name: Dan Taborda
Source: Sheet1 - Row 782
Comment: *I am submitting a number of feedback requests and would greatly appreciate being contacted or having a virtual meeting arranged to discuss them further. I would also be very happy to support any beta testing to help make this service even more efficient and sector-leading.

 *

 Currently, the Arbor Parent App does not allow parents and carers to communicate directly with individual teachers or relevant staff. The only option is the general in-app message, which redirects to the main school office inbox. This system is unsustainable, particularly for larger schools, as it creates unnecessary workload and delays in messages reaching the appropriate person.

 While parents can reply directly to staff if they receive an email sent via Arbor, this does not resolve the issue ‚Äî most families primarily use the Arbor App, and there is no in-app function to message staff directly.

 Key Benefits and Safeguarding Considerations:

 * Improved communication flow: Enables parents and carers to contact the relevant teacher, tutor, or pastoral lead directly through the app, ensuring messages reach the correct person quickly.

 * Reduced administrative workload: The main office would no longer need to triage and manually forward large volumes of messages.

 * Supports engagement and partnership: Strengthens school‚Äìhome collaboration through clear, direct, and traceable communication.

 * Safeguarding control: Each school should have full control over this feature including the ability to turn it on or off, set who can be contacted, and define whether replies are allowed.

 * Customisable permissions: Schools could choose to limit communication to specific staff groups (e.g. class teachers, Heads of Year, pastoral staff) in line with safeguarding and communication policies. However, schools must have the ability to toggle this feature on or off, restrict it etc.

 * Student App extension (optional): Similar functionality could be developed for the Student App, allowing teacher‚Äìstudent communication for homework or feedback. However, schools must have the ability to toggle this feature on or off, restrict it to teacher‚Äìstudent only, and disable student-to-student messaging entirely for safeguarding compliance.

 * Feature parity with previous systems: EduLink successfully offered this functionality, demonstrating it can be implemented securely and efficiently.

 Providing this flexibility, where schools control activation and permissions, would make Arbor far more functional, sustainable, and safeguarding-compliant, while significantly improving the quality of school‚Äìhome communication.
